</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Human Development Index</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_UN_Human_Development_Report_Quartiles.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/2014_UN_Human_Development_Report_Quartiles.svg/450px-2014_UN_Human_Development_Report_Quartiles.svg.png" width="450" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/2014_UN_Human_Development_Report_Quartiles.svg/675px-2014_UN_Human_Development_Report_Quartiles.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/2014_UN_Human_Development_Report_Quartiles.svg/900px-2014_UN_Human_Development_Report_Quartiles.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="863" data-file-height="375" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2014_UN_Human_Development_Report_Quartiles.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
World map indicating the categories of Human Development Index by country (based on 2013 data, published on July 24, 2014).
<table border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" style="width:100%; background:none;">

<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #3072D9; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;High</div>
</td>
<td valign="top">
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #A8C3FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Medium</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #E6EDFF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Low</div>
</td>
<td valign="top">
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #858585; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;No data</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>Human Development Index</b> (<b>HDI</b>) is a composite statistic of <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> indicators, which are used to rank countries into four tiers of <a href="/wiki/Human_development_(humanity)" title="Human development (humanity)">human development</a>. A country scores higher HDI when the <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" class="mw-redirect" title="Life expectancy at birth">lifespan</a> is higher, the <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a> level is higher, and the <a href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> is higher. The HDI was developed by the Pakistani economist <a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a> working alongside Indian economist <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a>, often framed in terms of whether people are able to "be" and "do" desirable things in their life, and was published by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a>.</p>
<p>The 2010 <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a> introduced an <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index</a> (IHDI). While the simple HDI remains useful, it stated that "the IHDI is the actual level of human development (accounting for <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">inequality</a>)," and "the HDI can be viewed as an index of 'potential' human development (or the maximum IHDI that could be achieved if there were no inequality)."</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg/175px-Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg" width="175" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg/263px-Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg/350px-Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg 2x" data-file-width="397" data-file-height="404" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mahbub-ul-Haq.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg/175px-Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg" width="175" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e0/Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="320" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amartya_Sen_NIH.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The origins of the HDI are found in the annual Human Development Reports produced by the Human Development Reports Office of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> (UNDP). These were devised and launched by Pakistani economist <a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a> in 1990, and had the explicit purpose "to shift the focus of development economics from <a href="/wiki/National_income" class="mw-redirect" title="National income">national income</a> accounting to people-centered policies". To produce the Human Development Reports, Mahbub ul Haq formed a group of development economists including <a href="/wiki/Paul_Streeten" title="Paul Streeten">Paul Streeten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frances_Stewart" title="Frances Stewart">Frances Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Ranis" title="Gustav Ranis">Gustav Ranis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Griffin_(economist)" title="Keith Griffin (economist)">Keith Griffin</a>, Sudhir Anand, and <a href="/wiki/Meghnad_Desai" class="mw-redirect" title="Meghnad Desai">Meghnad Desai</a>. Working alongside Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a>, they worked on capabilities and functions that provided the underlying conceptual framework. Haq believed that a simple composite measure of human development was needed to convince the public, academics, and politicians that they can and should evaluate development not only by economic advances but also improvements in human <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">well-being</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dimensions_and_calculation">Dimensions and calculation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Dimensions and calculation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_method_.282010_Index_onwards.29">New method (2010 Index onwards)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: New method (2010 Index onwards)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Published on 4 November 2010 (and updated on 10 June 2011), the 2010 Human Development Index (HDI) combines three dimensions:<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>A long and healthy life: Life expectancy at birth</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Education_index" class="mw-redirect" title="Education index">Education index</a>: Mean years of schooling and Expected years of schooling</li>
<li>A decent standard of living: <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">GNI</a> per capita (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a> US$)</li>
</ul>
<p>In its <a href="/wiki/2010_Human_Development_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 Human Development Report">2010 Human Development Report</a>, the UNDP began using a new method of calculating the HDI. The following three indices are used:</p>
<p>1.<span id="Life_Expectancy_Index"></span> Life Expectancy Index (LEI) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

                  <mtext>LE</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mn>20</mn>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>
              <mn>85</mn>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mn>20</mn>
            </mrow>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle ={\frac {{\textrm {LE}}-20}{85-20}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a222c3bdfb22ca9ff86d4861b5a7a35fac63925d" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:11.553ex; height:5.509ex;" alt="={\frac {{\textrm {LE}}-20}{85-20}}" /></span></p>
<dl>
<dd>
<dl>
<dd>LEI is 1 when Life expectancy at birth is 85 and 0 when Life expectancy at birth is 20.</dd>
</dl>
</dd>
</dl>
<p>2. <a href="/wiki/Education_Index" title="Education Index">Education Index</a> (EI) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>MYSI</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>+</mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>EYSI</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mrow>
            </mrow>
            <mn>2</mn>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle ={\frac {{\textrm {MYSI}}+{\textrm {EYSI}}}{2}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/322a300516420de9fa83acbd25f56e3f704e7ef8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:17.699ex; height:5.343ex;" alt="={\frac {{\textrm {MYSI}}+{\textrm {EYSI}}}{2}}" /></span></p>
<dl>
<dd>2.1 Mean Years of Schooling Index (MYSI) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mtext>MYS</mtext>
            </mrow>
            <mn>15</mn>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle ={\frac {\textrm {MYS}}{15}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/55aabf77d89eb9e57d504c519802826d7a7da917" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:8.498ex; height:5.509ex;" alt="={\frac {\textrm {MYS}}{15}}" /></span><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>
<dl>
<dd>Fifteen is the projected maximum of this indicator for 2025.</dd>
</dl>
</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>2.2 Expected Years of Schooling Index (EYSI) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mtext>EYS</mtext>
            </mrow>
            <mn>18</mn>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle ={\frac {\textrm {EYS}}{18}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d144416b4a2047923a6c231941cd3099f90fd5dd" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:7.95ex; height:5.509ex;" alt="={\frac {\textrm {EYS}}{18}}" /></span><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>
<dl>
<dd>Eighteen is equivalent to achieving a master's degree in most countries.</dd>
</dl>
</dd>
</dl>
<p>3. Income Index (II) <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>ln</mi>
              <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>GNIpc</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mi>ln</mi>
              <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
              <mn>100</mn>
              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>
              <mi>ln</mi>
              <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
              <mn>75</mn>
              <mo>,</mo>
              <mn>000</mn>
              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mi>ln</mi>
              <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
              <mo stretchy="false">(</mo>
              <mn>100</mn>
              <mo stretchy="false">)</mo>
            </mrow>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle ={\frac {\ln({\textrm {GNIpc}})-\ln(100)}{\ln(75,000)-\ln(100)}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1d31358617cecf8fc487c6db57b60f1864ab41c3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:24.159ex; height:6.509ex;" alt="={\frac {\ln({\textrm {GNIpc}})-\ln(100)}{\ln(75,000)-\ln(100)}}" /></span></p>
<dl>
<dd>
<dl>
<dd>II is 1 when GNI per capita is $75,000 and 0 when GNI per capita is $100.</dd>
</dl>
</dd>
</dl>
<p>Finally, the HDI is the <a href="/wiki/Geometric_mean" title="Geometric mean">geometric mean</a> of the previous three normalized indices:<br />
<span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mtext>HDI</mtext>
          </mrow>
        </mrow>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mroot>
            <mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>LEI</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>EI</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>&#x22C5;<!-- ⋅ --></mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mtext>II</mtext>
                </mrow>
              </mrow>
            </mrow>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mn>3</mn>
            </mrow>
          </mroot>
        </mrow>
        <mo>.</mo>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\textrm {HDI}}={\sqrt[{3}]{{\textrm {LEI}}\cdot {\textrm {EI}}\cdot {\textrm {II}}}}.}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/364ecd910bf260a13250cde6a9d25e08d9633fe8" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:21.531ex; height:3.009ex;" alt="{\textrm {HDI}}={\sqrt[{3}]{{\textrm {LEI}}\cdot {\textrm {EI}}\cdot {\textrm {II}}}}." /></span></p>
<p><small>LE: <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" class="mw-redirect" title="Life expectancy at birth">Life expectancy at birth</a><br />
MYS: Mean years of schooling (i.e. years that a person aged 25 or older has spent in formal education)<br />
EYS: Expected years of schooling (i.e. total expected years of schooling for children under 18 years of age)<br />
GNIpc: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GNI_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GNI (PPP) per capita">Gross national income at purchasing power parity per capita</a></small></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_method_.28before_2010_Index.29">Old method (before 2010 Index)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Old method (before 2010 Index)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The HDI combined three dimensions last used in its 2009 Report:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth, as an index of population health and longevity to HDI</li>
<li>Knowledge and education, as measured by the adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate (with two-thirds weighting) and the combined primary, secondary, and tertiary <a href="/wiki/Gross_enrollment_ratio" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross enrollment ratio">gross enrollment ratio</a> (with one-third weighting).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">Standard of living</a>, as indicated by the <a href="/wiki/Natural_logarithm" title="Natural logarithm">natural logarithm</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> <a href="/wiki/Per_capita" title="Per capita">per capita</a> at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Human_Development_Index_trends.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Human_Development_Index_trends.svg/280px-Human_Development_Index_trends.svg.png" width="280" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Human_Development_Index_trends.svg/420px-Human_Development_Index_trends.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Human_Development_Index_trends.svg/560px-Human_Development_Index_trends.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1179" data-file-height="1152" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Human_Development_Index_trends.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
HDI trends between 1975 and 2004
<table style="width:100%;">
<tr>

<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #FF0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> not in the OECD and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a></div>

</td>
<td valign="top">
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #00FF00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #003FD9; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a></div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C600FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a></div>
</td>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>This methodology was used by the UNDP until their 2011 report.</p>
<p>The formula defining the HDI is promulgated by the United Nations Development Programme (<a href="/wiki/UNDP" class="mw-redirect" title="UNDP">UNDP</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> In general, to transform a raw <a href="/wiki/Variable_(mathematics)" title="Variable (mathematics)">variable</a>, say <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.34ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="x" /></span>, into a unit-free <a href="/wiki/Index_(economics)" title="Index (economics)">index</a> between 0 and 1 (which allows different indices to be added together), the following <a href="/wiki/Formula" title="Formula">formula</a> is used:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mtext>&#xA0;index</mtext>
        </mrow>
        <mo>=</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>x</mi>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mi>a</mi>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>
              <mi>b</mi>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mi>a</mi>
            </mrow>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x{\text{ index}}={\frac {x-a}{b-a}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/649cc3be2e96c9683d44387a699f36a4269c22a5" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:16.841ex; height:4.843ex;" alt="{\displaystyle x{\text{ index}}={\frac {x-a}{b-a}}}" /></span></li>
</ul>
<p>where <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>a</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle a}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ffd2487510aa438433a2579450ab2b3d557e5edc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.24ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="a" /></span> and <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>b</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle b}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f11423fbb2e967f986e36804a8ae4271734917c3" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.008ex; height:2.176ex;" alt="b" /></span> are the <a href="/wiki/Maxima_and_minima" title="Maxima and minima">lowest and highest values</a> the variable <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mi>x</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.34ex; height:1.676ex;" alt="x" /></span> can attain, respectively.</p>
<p>The Human Development Index (HDI) then represents the uniformly weighted sum with ⅓ contributed by each of the following factor indices:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Life_Expectancy_Index" class="mw-redirect" title="Life Expectancy Index">Life Expectancy Index</a> = <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>L</mi>
              <mi>E</mi>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mn>25</mn>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>
              <mn>85</mn>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mn>25</mn>
            </mrow>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {LE-25}{85-25}}}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/40e4fa272c038fee629c7e37ff5fe5e656651dfc" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:9.412ex; height:5.509ex;" alt="{\frac {LE-25}{85-25}}" /></span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Education_Index" title="Education Index">Education Index</a> = <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mn>2</mn>
            <mn>3</mn>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>&#x00D7;<!-- × --></mo>
        <mi>A</mi>
        <mi>L</mi>
        <mi>I</mi>
        <mo>+</mo>
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mn>1</mn>
            <mn>3</mn>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
        <mo>&#x00D7;<!-- × --></mo>
        <mi>G</mi>
        <mi>E</mi>
        <mi>I</mi>
      </mstyle>
    </mrow>
    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {2}{3}}\times ALI+{\frac {1}{3}}\times GEI}</annotation>
  </semantics>
</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bb9ecff3db38a05ce742e739b634bd0f128b07e4" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:21.905ex; height:5.343ex;" alt="{\frac {2}{3}}\times ALI+{\frac {1}{3}}\times GEI" /></span>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adult_Literacy_Index" title="Adult Literacy Index">Adult Literacy Index</a> (ALI) = <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>A</mi>
              <mi>L</mi>

              <mn>0</mn>
            </mrow>
            <mrow>
              <mn>100</mn>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mn>0</mn>
            </mrow>
          </mfrac>
        </mrow>
      </mstyle>

    <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle {\frac {ALR-0}{100-0}}}</annotation>

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7269bb3957124db41f2af85a8d23c744239e7999" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:9.981ex; height:5.509ex;" alt="{\frac {ALR-0}{100-0}}" /></span></li>

</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> = <span class="mwe-math-element"><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" >
  <semantics>
    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
      <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
        <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
          <mfrac>
            <mrow>
              <mi>log</mi>
              <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
              <mrow>
                <mo>(</mo>
                <mi>G</mi>
                <mi>D</mi>
                <mi>P</mi>
                <mi>p</mi>
                <mi>c</mi>
                <mo>)</mo>
              </mrow>
              <mo>&#x2212;<!-- − --></mo>
              <mi>log</mi>
              <mo>&#x2061;<!-- ⁡ --></mo>
              <mrow>
                <mo>(</mo>
                <mn>100</mn>
                <mo>)</mo>
              </mrow>

</math></span><img src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/483e95e8d1b62061ec9f6ab0d4979f19e8d8e781" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" aria-hidden="true" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:24.597ex; height:6.509ex;" alt="{\frac {\log \left(GDPpc\right)-\log \left(100\right)}{\log \left(40000\right)-\log \left(100\right)}}" /></span></li>
</ul>
<p>Other organizations/companies may include other factors, such as infant mortality, which produces a different HDI.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_Human_Development_Index">2015 Human Development Index</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2015 Human Development Index">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>
<p>The 2015 Human Development Report by the United Nations Development Programme was released on December 14, 2015, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2014. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:<sup id="cite_ref-2015_Complete_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Complete-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Macau_in_Figures.2C_2015_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_in_Figures.2C_2015-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dgbas2011_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dgbas2011-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = decrease.</li>
<li>The number in brackets represents the number of ranks the country has climbed (up or down) relative to the ranking in the 2014 report.</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI">Inequality-adjusted HDI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Inequality-adjusted HDI">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI)<sup id="cite_ref-2015_Complete_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Complete-6">[6]</a></sup> is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account."</p>
<p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />) represent changes in rank. The rankings are not relative to the HDI list above due to the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data (p.&#160;216).</small></p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">

<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a missing IHDI: <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_Human_Development_Index">2014 Human Development Index</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2014 Human Development Index">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The 2014 Human Development Report by the United Nations Development Programme was released on July 24, 2014, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2013. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:<sup id="cite_ref-2014_Complete_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Complete-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Macau_in_Figures.2C_2015_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macau_in_Figures.2C_2015-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dgbas2011_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dgbas2011-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> = decrease.</li>
<li>The number in brackets represents the number of ranks the country has climbed (up or down) relative to the ranking in the 2013 report.</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_not_included">Countries not included</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Countries not included">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some countries were not included for various reasons, primarily due to the lack of necessary data. The following United Nations Member States were not included in the 2014 report:<sup id="cite_ref-2014_Complete_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Complete-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_2">Inequality-adjusted HDI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Inequality-adjusted HDI">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI)<sup id="cite_ref-2014_Complete_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_Complete-12">[12]</a></sup> is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account."</p>
<p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />) represent changes in rank. The rankings are not relative to the HDI list above due to the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data (p.&#160;168).</small></p>

<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a missing IHDI: <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_Human_Development_Index">2013 Human Development Index</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2013 Human Development Index">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>
<p>The 2013 Human Development Report by the United Nations Development Program was released on March 14, 2013, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2012. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Complete_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Complete-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />) represent changes in rank when compared to the new 2012 data HDI for 2011 – published in the 2012 report.</small></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_3">Inequality-adjusted HDI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Inequality-adjusted HDI">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI)<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Complete_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Complete-14">[14]</a></sup> is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account."</p>
<p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" title="Steady" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" />) represent changes in rank. The rankings are not relative to the HDI list above due to the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data (p.&#160;152).</small></p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">

<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a missing IHDI: <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_top_countries">Past top countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Past top countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The list below displays the top-ranked country from each year of the Human Development Index. <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> has been ranked the highest twelve times, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> eight times, followed by <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> which has been ranked highest three times. <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> has been ranked highest twice.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_each_original_HDI">In each original HDI</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: In each original HDI">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The year represents when the report was published. In parentheses is the year for which the index was calculated.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_coverage">Geographical coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Geographical coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The HDI has extended its geographical coverage: David Hastings, of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Commission_for_Asia_and_the_Pacific" title="United Nations Economic and Social Commission for Asia and the Pacific">United Nations Economic and Social Commission for Asia and the Pacific</a>, published a report geographically extending the HDI to 230+ economies, whereas the UNDP HDI for 2009 enumerates 182 economies and coverage for the 2010 HDI dropped to 169 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Country.2Fregion_specific_HDI_lists">Country/region specific HDI lists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Country/region specific HDI lists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Human_Development_Index&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg/220px-Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg/330px-Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg/440px-Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="522" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Human_welfare_and_ecological_footprint.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
HDI vs. <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Human Development Index has been criticized on a number of grounds including alleged ideological biases towards <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarianism</a> and so-called "<a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> <a href="/wiki/Economic_system" title="Economic system">models of development</a>", failure to include any <a href="/wiki/Ecological" class="mw-redirect" title="Ecological">ecological</a> considerations, lack of consideration of technological development or contributions to the human civilization, focusing exclusively on national performance and ranking, lack of attention to development from a global perspective, measurement error of the underlying statistics, and on the UNDP's changes in formula which can lead to severe misclassification in the categorisation of 'low', 'medium', 'high' or 'very high' human development countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolff_et_al._2011_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolff_et_al._2011-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Economists" class="mw-redirect" title="Economists">Economists</a> Hendrik Wolff, Howard Chong and <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Auffhammer" title="Maximilian Auffhammer">Maximilian Auffhammer</a> discuss the HDI from the perspective of data error in the underlying health, education and income statistics used to construct the HDI. They identified three sources of data error which are due to (i) data updating, (ii) formula revisions and (iii) thresholds to classify a country's development status and conclude that 11%, 21% and 34% of all countries can be interpreted as currently misclassified in the development bins due to the three sources of data error, respectively. The authors suggest that the United Nations should discontinue the practice of classifying countries into development bins because - they claim - the cut-off values seem arbitrary, can provide incentives for strategic behavior in reporting official statistics, and have the potential to misguide politicians, investors, charity donors and the public who use the HDI at large.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolff_et_al._2011_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolff_et_al._2011-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010 the UNDP reacted to the criticism and updated the thresholds to classify nations as low, medium, and high human development countries. In a comment to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> in early January 2011, the Human Development Report Office responded<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> to a January 6, 2011 article in the magazine<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> which discusses the Wolff <i>et al.</i> paper. The Human Development Report Office states that they undertook a systematic revision of the methods used for the calculation of the HDI and that the new methodology directly addresses the critique by Wolff <i>et al.</i> in that it generates a system for continuous updating of the human development categories whenever formula or data revisions take place.</p>

</div>

Taiwan's government calculated its HDI to be 0.882, based on 2010 new methodology of UNDP. <cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.dgbas.gov.tw/public/Data/491716362790WG0X9I.pdf">"2011中華民國人類發展指數 (HDI)"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span> (in Chinese). Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2011-11-21</span></span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+Development+Index&amp;rft.btitle=2011%E4%B8%E8%8F%AF%E6%B0%91%E5%9C%E4%BA%BA%E9%A1%9E%E7%99%BC%E5%B1%95%E6%8C%87%E6%95%B8+%28HDI%29&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.dgbas.gov.tw%2Fpublic%2FData%2F491716362790WG0X9I.pdf&amp;rft.pub=Directorate+General+of+Budget%2C+Accounting+and+Statistics%2C+Executive+Yuan%2C+R.O.C.&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>

<li><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hdr.undp.org/en/media/hdr_20072008_tech_note_1.pdf">"Technical note explaining the definition of the HDI"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHuman+Development+Index&amp;rft.btitle=Technical+note+explaining+the+definition+of+the+HDI&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fhdr.undp.org%2Fen%2Fmedia%2Fhdr_20072008_tech_note_1.pdf&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span>&#160;<small>(5.54&#160;MB)</small></li>

<li>An independent <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.humansecurityindex.org/?page_id=204">HDI</a> covering 232 countries, formulated along lines of the traditional (pre-2010) approach.</li>

<th scope="row" class="navbox-group"><a href="/wiki/Human_development_(humanity)" title="Human development (humanity)">Human development</a></th>

<th scope="row" class="navbox-group">General</th>
